## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the population growth rate (dP/dt) as a function of time (t) and current population size (P). This is a classic population dynamics problem where growth rate depends on population size through density-dependent feedback mechanisms, and possibly on time through seasonal or environmental forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Exponential (Malthusian) growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P', 'scenario': 'Density-independent growth where rate is proportional to population size'}
- {'name': 'Logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent growth with linear feedback (carrying capacity)'}
- {'name': 'Gompertz growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate decreasing logarithmically as population approaches carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Theta-logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)', 'scenario': 'Generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence controlled by exponent'}
- {'name': 'Allee effect growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P)', 'scenario': 'Population growth with a minimum viable population threshold (strong Allee effect)'}
- {'name': 'Richards growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) / c2', 'scenario': 'Flexible asymmetric sigmoidal growth model'}
- {'name': 'Von Bertalanffy-type growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Growth as balance between anabolic (power-law) and catabolic (linear) processes'}
- {'name': 'Power-law growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1', 'scenario': 'Generalized density-dependent growth with fractional exponent'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent logistic growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * t', 'scenario': 'Logistic growth with linearly changing environmental conditions'}
- {'name': 'Seasonally forced growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t))', 'scenario': 'Logistic growth modulated by periodic environmental forcing'}
- {'name': 'Quadratic density dependence', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3', 'scenario': 'Polynomial expansion of density-dependent growth rate'}
- {'name': 'Beverton-Holt continuous analog', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Growth with saturating reproduction minus density-dependent mortality'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent negative feedback → multiplicative factor (1 - c*P) or (1 - (c*P)**n) limiting growth at high P
- Allee effect (positive density dependence at low P) → additional multiplicative factor (P - c) introducing a lower critical threshold
- Logarithmic saturation → log(c/P) term producing slower approach to carrying capacity than polynomial models
- Metabolic scaling in growth → power-law terms P**c with fractional exponents (e.g., 2/3, 3/4) reflecting surface-to-volume relationships
- Environmental periodicity → sinusoidal modulation sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) multiplied with growth terms for seasonal effects
- Balance of gains and losses → difference of two power-law terms c0*P**a - c1*P**b representing anabolism vs catabolism
- Time-varying carrying capacity → carrying capacity parameter replaced by function of t (e.g., linear c0 + c1*t or exponential)

GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P/(c4 + exp(-c5*(-c6 + P)))

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.1728*(1 - P/48.55)*P + 0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*(-0.924 + P)))`

This simplifies to:
- Term 1: `c0*P - c0*P²/c2` = quadratic in P (specifically `0.1728*P - 0.003559*P²`)
- Term 2: `c3*P/(1 + exp(-c5*(P - c6)))` = P times a sigmoid function

So GT = `a*P + b*P² + c*P/(1 + exp(-d*(P - e)))` where a, b are specific constants.

The key structural elements are:
1. A polynomial part: `c0*P*(1 - P/c2)` = linear + quadratic in P
2. A sigmoidal part: `c3*P/(1 + exp(-c5*(P-c6)))`

Note that `log(k*exp(x) + 1)` is a softplus function, and its derivative is a sigmoid. Also, `tanh` can approximate a sigmoid but is NOT exactly equal to one.

Let me check key candidates:

**Candidates with `log(c*exp(P*c) + 1)` terms** - these are softplus functions, NOT sigmoids. The GT has a sigmoid `1/(1+exp(-x))`. These are fundamentally different functions. A softplus is the integral of a sigmoid. So candidates using `log(c*exp(P*c)+1)` would need to somehow produce a sigmoid through their structure.

Wait - let me reconsider. The GT has `P/(1 + exp(-c5*(P-c6)))`. Can `log(a*exp(bP)+1)` produce this? No, these are different basis functions.

**Candidates with `tanh`**: Note that `tanh(x) = 2*sigmoid(2x) - 1`, so `sigmoid(x) = (1 + tanh(x/2))/2`. Thus `P/(1+exp(-x)) = P*(1+tanh(x/2))/2 = P/2 + P*tanh(x/2)/2`.

So GT = `a*P² + b*P + c*P*(1+tanh(d*(P-e)/2))/2` = `a*P² + (b+c/2)*P + (c/2)*P*tanh(d*(P-e)/2)`

**Candidate 42:** `P*c0*(P*c1 + 1) + c2*tanh(P*c3 + c4)`
= `c0*c1*P² + c0*P + c2*tanh(c3*P + c4)`

GT needs `P*tanh(...)`, but this has just `tanh(...)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 51:** `P*c0*(P + c1) + c2*tanh(P*c3 + c4)`
= `c0*P² + c0*c1*P + c2*tanh(c3*P+c4)` - same issue, needs P*tanh, has tanh. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 52:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + c2*tanh(P*c3 + c4)` - same structure. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 53:** `P*c0 + P*c1*(P+c2) + c3*tanh(P*c4+c5)` - same. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 2:** `P*c0 + c1*tanh(P*c2+c3) + c4*log(c5*exp(P*c6)+1)` - no P² term possible without P*tanh or P*softplus. **NO MATCH**

Let me check candidates with `sin` - these can't match sigmoid. **NO MATCH** for all pure sin candidates.

**Candidates 58-68** are polynomials - can't match sigmoid. **NO MATCH**

After careful analysis, none of the candidates can produce the `P*sigmoid(P)` term that appears in the GT. The sigmoid/softplus/tanh functions in candidates either lack the P multiplier or use wrong basis functions.
